I want to make something akin to trinket.io -- they let you make Python programs and run them, but unless you pay, you can only save python2 programs. I would like to make a version of that that lets you do python3. But I also want to do it using pyolite -- the wasm python -- so everything can happen in the browser. I'd like to use an open-source editor component (maybe Ace?), and we can save to a sqlite db in ./data

Let's write it in Go -- we can use the "single goroutine does all the DB access" pattern to keep safe. Please ask me questions until you have a good idea of the design, then we'll make a plan and save it in PLAN.md

Excellent! I'm getting a clearer picture. A few more questions:

Google OAuth

Yes, you'll need to create a free Google Cloud project and set up OAuth 2.0 credentials. The steps are:

  1. Go to Google Cloud Console
  2. Create a new project (free)
  3. Enable the "Google+ API" or "People API"
  4. Create OAuth 2.0 credentials (Client ID and Secret)
  5. Set authorized redirect URIs (e.g., http://localhost:8080/auth/callback)

Question: Do you want me to include detailed setup instructions in the plan, or just note "requires Google OAuth setup" and you'll handle it?

Ok, for Google login, I created an OAuth 2.0 Client ID:

  • Cliend ID: [REDACTED-GOOGLE-CLIENT-ID]
  • Authorized JavaScript origins: http://localhost:3000
  • Authorized redirect URIs: http://localhost:3000/auth/callback
  • Client secret: in 1password (can be read with op read "op://Shared/Trifle Web Client for Google OAuth/credential")

The allowlist should be in the sqlite DB. We can do flat list of trifles for now. Layout sounds good. main.py sounds good. No sharing yet.

One note: I've learned from hard experience that you should never tie your logins/users directly to your accounts in the DB. As an example: YouTube started out with username==login==channel. But a famous musician might want to let multiple people manage the channel, and they each need their own login. So I think it's best to separate them in the DB from the start, but not expose that in the UI at all: just keep looking how it would have looked if user==login==account==everythingelse. Does that make sense? The only reason I think this is worth considering is if we eventually develop a concept of a shared account, that eg. multiple teachers, or a teach and an assistant might share. But for now, it should look like it's just one thing. Please ask me questions if anything is unclear here.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-18 20:17:57

üí≠ Thinking

This is great! The user has provided a lot of clarity. Let me understand the user/account separation:

  • Login: The Google OAuth identity (email, OAuth ID)
  • Account: The entity that owns Trifles
  • Membership: A join table between Logins and Accounts

So the DB might look like:

  • logins table: id, google_id, email, created_at
  • accounts table: id, name (or display_name), created_at
  • account_members table: account_id, login_id, role (owner/editor), created_at
  • trifles table: id, account_id, name, created_at, ...

For now, when a user logs in for the first time, we:

  1. Create a Login record
  2. Create an Account record (maybe named after their email or "My Trifles")
  3. Link them with account_members (as owner)
  4. In the UI, they just see "their" Trifles - no concept of accounts/teams exposed

Later, we could add UI to invite others to an account, etc.

This is a smart pattern! It gives flexibility later without having to migrate data.

Let me confirm my understanding and ask about auto-save.

I'll focus on the user interface and system architecture. The UI will have a clean, functional design with a top navbar featuring user options and a "New Trifle" button. A left sidebar will display the file tree for the current Trifle, while the main area will be split between the code editor and an output console. Users can easily browse their Trifles in a dedicated view.

The backend will use a single goroutine for database access, ensuring thread-safe operations through a channel-based approach. The Go server will efficiently serve embedded static files, and all Python code execution will happen client-side using Pyodide in the browser.

Primary key\n- `account_id` - Foreign key to accounts\n- `login_id` - Foreign key to logins\n- `role` - Role string (e.g., \"owner\", \"editor\") - just \"owner\" for V1\n- `created_at` - Timestamp\n- Unique constraint on (account_id, login_id)\n\n#### `trifles`\nIndividual Python projects/programs\n- `id` - Primary key (random short hex ID, e.g., \"a3f9c2\")\n- `account_id` - Foreign key to accounts\n- `title` - User-provided title\n- `description` - Optional description\n- `parent_id` - Foreign key to trifles (for future cloning/remixing, nullable)\n- `created_at` - Timestamp\n- `updated_at` - Timestamp\n\n#### `trifle_files`\nFiles within a Trifle (supports folders via path)\n- `id` - Primary key\n- `trifle_id` - Foreign key to trifles\n- `path` - File path within project (e.g., \"main.py\", \"utils/helper.py\")\n- `content` - File contents (text)\n- `created_at` - Timestamp\n- `updated_at` - Timestamp\n- Unique constraint on (trifle_id, path)\n\n#### `email_allowlist`\nControls who can log in\n- `id` - Primary key\n- `pattern` - Email or domain pattern (e.g., \"[REDACTED-EMAIL]\" or \"@misstudent.com\")\n- `type` - \"email\" or \"domain\"\n- `created_at` - Timestamp\n- Unique constraint on (pattern, type)\n\n### Initial Allowlist Data\n- Individual email: `[REDACTED-EMAIL]`\n- Domain: `@misstudent.com`\n\n## Architecture\n\n### Backend (Go)\n\n**Pattern**: Single goroutine handles all database access via channels to ensure thread safety.\n\n**Key Components**:\n1. **Database Manager Goroutine**:\n   - Runs in background, receives requests via channel\n   - Executes all SQLite operations\n   - Returns results via response channels\n\n2. **HTTP Server**:\n   - Serves embedded static files\n   - Provides API endpoints\n   - Handles OAuth flow\n\n3. **OAuth Handler**:\n   - Initiates Google OAuth flow\n   - Handles callback\n   - Verifies email against allowlist BEFORE creating session\n   - Creates Login + Account + AccountMember on first login\n   - Generates adjective-noun display name (ensures uniqueness)\n\n4. **Session Management**:\n   - Use secure HTTP-only cookies\n   - Session data in memory (or SQLite if preferred)\n\n### Frontend (Vanilla JS)\n\n**Pages/Views**:\n1. **Login Page**: Google Sign-In button\n2. **Trifle List**: Browse user's Trifles, create new\n3. **Trifle Editor**: Main workspace\n\n**Trifle Editor Layout**:\n```\n+----------------------------------------------------------+\n|  Navbar: [Trifle Logo] [Title]           [User] [Logout]|\n+----------------------------------------------------------+\n| File    |                                                 |\n| Tree    |  Ace Editor                                     |\n|         |  (resizable)                                    |\n|  \ud83d\udcc1 /   |                                                 |\n|  \ud83d\udcc4main.|                                                 |\n|  \ud83d\udcc4util.|                                                 |\n|         +--------------------------------------------------+\n|         |  Output Console                                 |\n|         |  (Python stdout/stderr)                         |\n|         |  [Run Button]                                   |\n+---------+--------------------------------------------------+\n```\n\n**Key Frontend Features**:\n- Ace Editor with Python syntax highlighting\n- File tree with add/delete/rename files\n- Resizable editor/console split\n- \"Run\" button executes main.py via Pyodide\n- Auto-save (debounced, triggers ~1s after typing stops)\n- Load Ace and Pyodide from CDNs\n\n## API Endpoints\n\n### Authentication\n- `GET /auth/login` - Admin interface for managing allowlist?\n\n## Notes\n\n- Ace Editor: https://ace.c9.io/ (can load from CDN)\n- Pyodide: https://pyodide.org/ (can load from CDN)\n- Keep UI simple and clean, inspired by trinket.io\n- Auto-save eliminates \"run unsaved code\" issues\n- Short hex IDs for Trifles (e.g., 6 chars = 16M possibilities)\n"

üë§ USER ‚Äî 2025-10-18 20:38:52

Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

That looks great. A few notes and further things that came to mind:

  1. I plan on hosting this with Caddy terminating TLS, on https://trifle.greenseptember.com
  2. Go 1.25 has a modern XSRF prevention middleware that is :fire: -- You can read https://www.alexedwards.net/blog/preventing-csrf-in-go
  3. Do we have any call to use https://pkg.go.dev/crawshaw.io/sqlite or would it be better to try to keep our SQL generic so that we could use almost any DB? I think the latter.
  4. I'm a huge fan of "SQL is great for SQL; let's just keep all of it in one place", so let's use sqlc and make sure all the SQL is confined to one package.
  5. Any time trifle IDs or user IDs or anything are exposed in our API, let's do that stripe/github-flavored thing of using prefixes. So, trifle_123ABC, account_123ABC, etc.
  6. Oh, and let's make any exposed ID a random string of hex digits: no German Tank Problem gonna happen on our watch!

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-18 20:38:59

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 2 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

üí≠ Thinking

Great feedback! Let me address each point:

  1. Hosting with Caddy - good to know, means we don't need to worry about TLS in the Go app
  2. Go 1.23 (not 1.25, but I think they meant the latest) has new CSRF middleware - excellent, we should use that
  3. They're asking about using crawshaw.io/sqlite vs generic SQL. I think they're right - keeping it generic with database/sql and a driver like modernc.org/sqlite or mattn/go-sqlite3 is better for flexibility
  4. sqlc - great choice! This will generate type-safe Go code from SQL queries. All SQL goes in .sql files
  5. Prefixed IDs like Stripe - trifle_xxx, account_xxx, etc. Good for debugging and type safety
  6. Random hex strings for IDs - not sequential, prevents enumeration attacks

I should update the PLAN.md with these decisions.

     1‚Üí# Trifle - Browser-based Python3 Playground
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíA web application for creating, editing, and running Python3 programs entirely in the browser using Pyodide (WebAssembly Python).
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Project Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚Üí**Name**: Trifle (individual programs are called "Trifles")
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí**Core Concept**: Like trinket.io, but:
    10‚Üí- Python3 only (no Python2)
    11‚Üí- Runs entirely in browser via Pyodide
    12‚Üí- Open-source editor (Ace)
    13‚Üí- Restricted to allowlisted users
    14‚Üí- Multiple files per project
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí## Tech Stack
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üí- **Backend**: Go
    19‚Üí- **Frontend**: Vanilla JavaScript (consider htmx if it fits)
    20‚Üí- **Editor**: Ace Editor (from CDN)
    21‚Üí- **Python Runtime**: Pyodide (WebAssembly, from CDN)
    22‚Üí- **Database**: SQLite (file in `./data/trifle.db`)
    23‚Üí- **Authentication**: Google OAuth 2.0
    24‚Üí- **Deployment**: Single Go binary with embedded static files
    25‚Üí
    26‚Üí## Google OAuth Configuration
    27‚Üí
    28‚Üí- **Client ID**: `[REDACTED-GOOGLE-CLIENT-ID]`
    29‚Üí- **Client Secret**: Stored in 1Password, read via: `op read "op://Shared/Trifle Web Client for Google OAuth/credential"`
    30‚Üí- **Authorized Origins**: `http://localhost:3000`
    31‚Üí- **Redirect URI**: `http://localhost:3000/auth/callback`
    32‚Üí
    33‚Üí## Data Model
    34‚Üí
    35‚Üí### Tables
    36‚Üí
    37‚Üí#### `logins`
    38‚ÜíRepresents Google OAuth identities
    39‚Üí- `id` - Primary key
    40‚Üí- `google_id` - Unique Google user ID
    41‚Üí- `email` - User's email address
    42‚Üí- `name` - Display name from Google
    43‚Üí- `created_at` - Timestamp
    44‚Üí
    45‚Üí#### `accounts`
    46‚ÜíRepresents entities that own Trifles (separated from logins for future multi-user support)
    47‚Üí- `id` - Primary key
    48‚Üí- `display_name` - Auto-generated adjective-noun name (e.g., "purple-dinosaur")
    49‚Üí- `created_at` - Timestamp
    50‚Üí- `updated_at` - Timestamp
    51‚Üí
    52‚Üí#### `account_members`
    53‚ÜíLinks logins to accounts (one-to-one in V1, but designed for future multi-user)
    54‚Üí- `id` - Primary key
    55‚Üí- `account_id` - Foreign key to accounts
    56‚Üí- `login_id` - Foreign key to logins
    57‚Üí- `role` - Role string (e.g., "owner", "editor") - just "owner" for V1
    58‚Üí- `created_at` - Timestamp
    59‚Üí- Unique constraint on (account_id, login_id)
    60‚Üí
    61‚Üí#### `trifles`
    62‚ÜíIndividual Python projects/programs
    63‚Üí- `id` - Primary key (random short hex ID, e.g., "a3f9c2")
    64‚Üí- `account_id` - Foreign key to accounts
    65‚Üí- `title` - User-provided title
    66‚Üí- `description` - Optional description
    67‚Üí- `parent_id` - Foreign key to trifles (for future cloning/remixing, nullable)
    68‚Üí- `created_at` - Timestamp
    69‚Üí- `updated_at` - Timestamp
    70‚Üí
    71‚Üí#### `trifle_files`
    72‚ÜíFiles within a Trifle (supports folders via path)
    73‚Üí- `id` - Primary key
    74‚Üí- `trifle_id` - Foreign key to trifles
    75‚Üí- `path` - File path within project (e.g., "main.py", "utils/helper.py")
    76‚Üí- `content` - File contents (text)
    77‚Üí- `created_at` - Timestamp
    78‚Üí- `updated_at` - Timestamp
    79‚Üí- Unique constraint on (trifle_id, path)
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üí#### `email_allowlist`
    82‚ÜíControls who can log in
    83‚Üí- `id` - Primary key
    84‚Üí- `pattern` - Email or domain pattern (e.g., "[REDACTED-EMAIL]" or "@misstudent.com")
    85‚Üí- `type` - "email" or "domain"
    86‚Üí- `created_at` - Timestamp
    87‚Üí- Unique constraint on (pattern, type)
    88‚Üí
    89‚Üí### Initial Allowlist Data
    90‚Üí- Individual email: `[REDACTED-EMAIL]`
    91‚Üí- Domain: `@misstudent.com`
    92‚Üí
    93‚Üí## Architecture
    94‚Üí
    95‚Üí### Backend (Go)
    96‚Üí
    97‚Üí**Pattern**: Single goroutine handles all database access via channels to ensure thread safety.
    98‚Üí
    99‚Üí**Key Components**:
   100‚Üí1. **Database Manager Goroutine**:
   101‚Üí   - Runs in background, receives requests via channel
   102‚Üí   - Executes all SQLite operations
   103‚Üí   - Returns results via response channels
   104‚Üí
   105‚Üí2. **HTTP Server**:
   106‚Üí   - Serves embedded static files
   107‚Üí   - Provides API endpoints
   108‚Üí   - Handles OAuth flow
   109‚Üí
   110‚Üí3. **OAuth Handler**:
   111‚Üí   - Initiates Google OAuth flow
   112‚Üí   - Handles callback
   113‚Üí   - Verifies email against allowlist BEFORE creating session
   114‚Üí   - Creates Login + Account + AccountMember on first login
   115‚Üí   - Generates adjective-noun display name (ensures uniqueness)
   116‚Üí
   117‚Üí4. **Session Management**:
   118‚Üí   - Use secure HTTP-only cookies
   119‚Üí   - Session data in memory (or SQLite if preferred)
   120‚Üí
   121‚Üí### Frontend (Vanilla JS)
   122‚Üí
   123‚Üí**Pages/Views**:
   124‚Üí1. **Login Page**: Google Sign-In button
   125‚Üí2. **Trifle List**: Browse user's Trifles, create new
   126‚Üí3. **Trifle Editor**: Main workspace
   127‚Üí
   128‚Üí**Trifle Editor Layout**:
   129‚Üí```
   130‚Üí+----------------------------------------------------------+
   131‚Üí|  Navbar: [Trifle Logo] [Title]           [User] [Logout]|
   132‚Üí+----------------------------------------------------------+
   133‚Üí| File    |                                                 |
   134‚Üí| Tree    |  Ace Editor                                     |
   135‚Üí|         |  (resizable)                                    |
   136‚Üí|  üìÅ /   |                                                 |
   137‚Üí|  üìÑmain.|                                                 |
   138‚Üí|  üìÑutil.|                                                 |
   139‚Üí|         +--------------------------------------------------+
   140‚Üí|         |  Output Console                                 |
   141‚Üí|         |  (Python stdout/stderr)                         |
   142‚Üí|         |  [Run Button]                                   |
   143‚Üí+---------+--------------------------------------------------+
   144‚Üí```
   145‚Üí
   146‚Üí**Key Frontend Features**:
   147‚Üí- Ace Editor with Python syntax highlighting
   148‚Üí- File tree with add/delete/rename files
   149‚Üí- Resizable editor/console split
   150‚Üí- "Run" button executes main.py via Pyodide
   151‚Üí- Auto-save (debounced, triggers ~1s after typing stops)
   152‚Üí- Load Ace and Pyodide from CDNs
   153‚Üí
   154‚Üí## API Endpoints
   155‚Üí
   156‚Üí### Authentication
   157‚Üí- `GET /auth/login` - Redirect to Google OAuth
   158‚Üí- `GET /auth/callback` - OAuth callback, verify allowlist, create session
   159‚Üí- `POST /auth/logout` - Clear session
   160‚Üí
   161‚Üí### Account Management
   162‚Üí- `POST /api/account/reroll-name` - Generate new display name
   163‚Üí
   164‚Üí### Trifles
   165‚Üí- `GET /api/trifles` - List all user's Trifles
   166‚Üí- `POST /api/trifles` - Create new Trifle (returns ID)
   167‚Üí- `GET /api/trifles/:id` - Get Trifle metadata + all files
   168‚Üí- `PUT /api/trifles/:id` - Update Trifle metadata (title, description)
   169‚Üí- `DELETE /api/trifles/:id` - Delete Trifle
   170‚Üí
   171‚Üí### Trifle Files
   172‚Üí- `GET /api/trifles/:id/files` - List all files in Trifle
   173‚Üí- `PUT /api/trifles/:id/files` - Batch update files (for auto-save)
   174‚Üí- `POST /api/trifles/:id/files` - Create new file
   175‚Üí- `DELETE /api/trifles/:id/files` - Delete file (by path in query param)
   176‚Üí
   177‚Üí## Execution Model
   178‚Üí
   179‚Üí- All Python code runs **client-side** via Pyodide
   180‚Üí- No server-side Python execution
   181‚Üí- Output captured and displayed in console
   182‚Üí- `main.py` is the entry point when "Run" is clicked
   183‚Üí- Future: Support for micropip to install packages
   184‚Üí
   185‚Üí## V1 Scope (MVP)
   186‚Üí
   187‚Üí### Included
   188‚Üí‚úÖ Google OAuth login with allowlist enforcement
   189‚Üí‚úÖ Reject disallowed emails immediately (no access request page)

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-18 21:30:36

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 4 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

üí≠ Thinking

The user wants to use YouTube's method for ID conversion - using 3DES to encrypt/decrypt 64-bit integers. This is clever because:

  1. 3DES block size is 64 bits
  2. You can reversibly convert a database integer ID to a random-looking string
  3. No need to store the external ID in the database
  4. With the secret key, you can decrypt back to the original integer

For 3DES, you need a 24-byte (192-bit) key. The user wants a CLI command to generate this.

A good way to generate a random key is using openssl rand:

  • For 3DES, we need 24 bytes
  • We can encode as hex (48 hex digits) or base64

Let me provide a simple command to generate a 24-byte random key.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-18 21:30:41

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 4 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

Great idea! That's much cleaner - no need to store external IDs in the DB at all, and it's reversible.

For 3DES, you need a 24-byte (192-bit) key. Here's the command to generate one:

openssl rand -hex 24

This will output 48 hex characters (24 bytes).

If you prefer base64 encoding (shorter):

openssl rand -base64 24

This outputs 32 base64 characters.

I'd recommend hex for consistency with how you're already storing the OAuth secret. Want me to update the plan to reflect:

  1. The new 1Password path for the OAuth secret
  2. The addition of a 3DES secret for ID encryption
  3. The ID conversion approach (encrypt 64-bit DB ID ‚Üí hex string with prefix, decrypt back for lookups)

üë§ USER ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:05:28

I don't think you can decrypt with DES3 unless you have all 64 bits. Maybe we should just create hex IDs from the start? What do you think?

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:05:38

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 2 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

üí≠ Thinking

You're absolutely right! 3DES operates on 64-bit blocks, so you can't use it for shorter IDs like the 12-hex-char (48-bit) trifle IDs I suggested.

The user is asking whether we should just use random hex IDs from the start instead of trying to encrypt database integer IDs.

Let me think about the trade-offs:

3DES approach (YouTube method):

  • Pros: Reversible, no need to store external IDs, can use integer PKs in DB
  • Cons: All IDs must be exactly 64 bits (16 hex chars), can't have shorter IDs for URLs

Random hex from start:

  • Pros: Can choose any length we want, simpler code, no encryption needed
  • Cons: Need to store the random ID in DB, need uniqueness checks on insert

Actually, I think random hex from the start is simpler and more flexible. We can:

  • Use shorter IDs for trifles (better for URLs)
  • Use longer IDs for other entities if needed
  • No crypto dependency
  • Standard practice (like UUIDs but shorter)

The only downside is we need to store them and check uniqueness, but that's straightforward with a UNIQUE constraint.

Let me suggest this approach to the user.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:05:44

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 570 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

You're absolutely right! 3DES requires the full 64-bit block for decryption, so we can't do shorter IDs for trifles.

I think random hex IDs from the start is actually simpler and more flexible:

Pros:

  • Choose any length per entity type (short trifle IDs for nice URLs, longer for others)
  • No crypto dependency or key management for IDs
  • Simpler code - just generate random hex on insert
  • Standard approach (like short UUIDs)

Cons:

  • Store the ID string in DB (with UNIQUE constraint)
  • Check for collisions on insert (retry if collision, though extremely rare)

Proposed ID lengths:

  • trifle_ + 8 hex chars = 12 total chars (nice short URLs, 4 billion possibilities)
  • account_ + 12 hex chars (68 billion possibilities)
  • login_ + 12 hex chars
  • file_ + 12 hex chars

Still use the prefixes for type safety in logs/debugging. Store the full prefixed ID in the database.

Sound good?

   129‚Üí## Architecture
   130‚Üí
   131‚Üí### Backend (Go)
   132‚Üí
   133‚Üí**Pattern**: Single goroutine handles all database access via channels to ensure thread safety.
   134‚Üí
   135‚Üí**Database Access Strategy**:
   136‚Üí- Use [sqlc](https://sqlc.dev/) for type-safe, generated Go code from SQL
   137‚Üí- All SQL queries in one package (`internal/db/queries.sql`)
   138‚Üí- Schema migrations in `internal/db/schema.sql`
   139‚Üí- Generic SQL where possible (avoid SQLite-specific features) for future DB portability
   140‚Üí- Generated code handles parameter binding and row scanning
   141‚Üí
   142‚Üí**Key Components**:
   143‚Üí1. **Database Manager Goroutine**:
   144‚Üí   - Runs in background, receives requests via channel
   145‚Üí   - Executes all SQLite operations using sqlc-generated code
   146‚Üí   - Returns results via response channels
   147‚Üí
   148‚Üí2. **ID Generation**:
   149‚Üí   - Cryptographically random hex strings with type prefixes
   150‚Üí   - Helper functions in `internal/db/ids.go`
   151‚Üí   - Collision retry logic (though extremely rare)
   152‚Üí
   153‚Üí3. **HTTP Server**:
   154‚Üí   - Serves embedded static files
   155‚Üí   - Provides API endpoints
   156‚Üí   - Handles OAuth flow
   157‚Üí   - Uses Go 1.25 CSRF middleware
   158‚Üí
   159‚Üí4. **OAuth Handler**:
   160‚Üí   - Initiates Google OAuth flow
   161‚Üí   - Handles callback
   162‚Üí   - Verifies email against allowlist BEFORE creating session
   163‚Üí   - Creates Login + Account + AccountMember on first login
   164‚Üí   - Generates adjective-noun display name (ensures uniqueness)
   165‚Üí
   166‚Üí5. **Session Management**:
   167‚Üí   - Use secure HTTP-only cookies
   168‚Üí   - Session data in memory (or SQLite if preferred)
   169‚Üí

btw, how do folks usually do DB migrations in Go? Is there a generally agreed-upon standard? Or should we just do it ourselves by having a table with one row with one column showing DB version, and then just manually write migrations?

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:10:20

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 2 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

üí≠ Thinking

Good question about database migrations in Go. Let me think about the common approaches:

  1. golang-migrate/migrate - This is probably the most popular standalone migration tool for Go. It's very widely used and well-maintained.

  2. goose - Another popular option, simpler than migrate, also widely used.

  3. Tern - PostgreSQL-focused migration tool.

  4. sql-migrate - Another option, uses go-bindata to embed migrations.

  5. Manual versioning - What the user suggested - a version table and manual migration code.

  6. Atlas - More modern, works well with sqlc, declarative schema approach.

For this project, given that we're using sqlc and want to keep things simple, I think the user's manual approach could work fine for a small project. However, the popular libraries like golang-migrate or goose are battle-tested and handle edge cases well.

Since we're using sqlc, there's also Atlas which is from the same team and works really well with sqlc - it can do declarative schema management.

Let me give a balanced answer about the options.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:10:29

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 5 in / 2 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

Great question! There are a few common approaches:

Popular Migration Libraries

  1. golang-migrate/migrate - Most popular

    • Supports many databases
    • CLI tool + Go library
    • Up/down migrations in separate .sql files
    • Tracks version in schema_migrations table
    • Very battle-tested

  2. pressly/goose - Also very popular

    • Simpler than migrate
    • Supports SQL or Go migrations
    • Can embed migrations in binary
    • Good for our use case

  3. Atlas - Modern, works great with sqlc

    • Declarative schema approach (define target state, it figures out migrations)
    • Made by same team as sqlc
    • Can also do versioned migrations
    • Might be overkill for small project

Manual Approach

Your idea works fine for simple projects:

  • schema_version table with current version
  • Array/map of migration functions in code
  • Run migrations on startup if version < latest

Pros: No dependencies, full control Cons: You handle all edge cases (concurrent migrations, partial failures, etc.)

My Recommendation

For this project, I'd suggest goose because:

  • Simple and lightweight
  • Works great with sqlc (many sqlc users use it)
  • Migrations can be embedded in the binary
  • Well-tested edge case handling
  • Not over-engineered

We'd add migration files like:

internal/db/migrations/
  00001_initial_schema.sql
  00002_add_something.sql

Want to go with goose, or prefer the manual approach?

migrations/*.sql\nvar embedMigrations embed.FS\n\n// Manager handles all database operations through a single goroutine\ntype Manager struct {\n\tdb      *sql.DB\n\tqueries *Queries\n\treqCh   chan dbRequest\n\tcloseCh chan struct{}\n}\n\n// dbRequest represents a database operation request\ntype dbRequest struct {\n\tfn     func(*sql.DB, *Queries) (interface{}, error)\n\trespCh chan dbResponse\n}\n\n// dbResponse contains the result of a database operation\ntype dbResponse struct {\n\tresult interface{}\n\terr    error\n}\n\n// NewManager creates a new database manager and starts the worker goroutine\nfunc NewManager(dbPath string) (*Manager, error) {\n\tdb, err := sql.Open(\"sqlite\", dbPath)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to open database: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Enable foreign keys (disabled by default in SQLite)\n\tif _, err := db.Exec(\"PRAGMA foreign_keys = ON\"); err != nil {\n\t\tdb.Close()\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to enable foreign keys: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\t// Run migrations\n\tgoose.SetBaseFS(embedMigrations)\n\tif err := goose.SetDialect(\"sqlite3\"); err != nil {\n\t\tdb.Close()\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to set goose dialect: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tif err := goose.Up(db, \"migrations\"); err != nil {\n\t\tdb.Close()\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"failed to run migrations: %w\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tqueries := New(db)\n\n\tm := &Manager{\n\t\tdb:      db,\n\t\tqueries: queries,\n\t\treqCh:   make(chan dbRequest, 100), // Buffer for performance\n\t\tcloseCh: make(chan struct{}),\n\t}\n\n\t// Start the worker goroutine\n\tgo m.worker()\n\n\treturn m, nil\n}\n\n// worker is the single goroutine that handles all database operations\nfunc (m *Manager) worker() {\n\tfor {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase req := <-m.reqCh:\n\t\t\tresult, err := req.fn(m.db, m.queries)\n\t\t\treq.respCh <- dbResponse{result: result, err: err}\n\t\tcase <-m.closeCh:\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// execute sends a request to the worker goroutine and waits for the response\nfunc (m *Manager) execute(fn func(*sql.DB, *Queries) (interface{}, error)) (interface{}, error) {\n\trespCh := make(chan dbResponse, 1)\n\treq := dbRequest{\n\t\tfn:     fn,\n\t\trespCh: respCh,\n\t}\n\n\tm.reqCh <- req\n\tresp := <-respCh\n\treturn resp.result, resp.err\n}\n\n// Close shuts down the database manager\nfunc (m *Manager) Close() error {\n\tclose(m.closeCh)\n\treturn m.db.Close()\n}\n\n// Example methods - these demonstrate how to use the manager pattern\n// More methods will be added as needed\n\n// GetLoginByGoogleID retrieves a login by Google ID\nfunc (m *Manager) GetLoginByGoogleID(ctx context.Context, googleID string) (*Login, error) {\n\tresult, err := m.execute(func(db *sql.DB, q *Queries) (interface{}, operations in a transaction\nfunc (m *Manager) Transaction(ctx context.Context, fn func(*sql.Tx, *Queries) error) error {\n\t_, err := m.execute(func(db *sql.DB, q *Queries) (interface{}, error) {\n\t\ttx, err := db.BeginTx(ctx, nil)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tqtx := q.WithTx(tx)\n\n\t\terr = fn(tx, qtx)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tif rbErr := tx.Rollback(); rbErr != nil {\n\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"rollback error: %v (original error: %v)\", rbErr, err)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif err := tx.Commit(); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil, err\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t})\n\treturn err\n}\n"

üí≠ Thinking

Ah, I see! The issue is that modernc.org/sqlite and modernc.org/libc need to be kept in sync. The problem occurs when someone updates libc to a newer version than what sqlite was built with, which can cause type incompatibility errors.

The solution recommended by the maintainer is to use the same version of modernc.org/libc that's specified in modernc.org/sqlite's go.mod.

Since we're using modernc.org/sqlite v1.39.1, I should check what version of libc it requires and make sure that's what we have. I already checked earlier and they match (v1.66.10), so we're good. But I should add a comment in the go.mod or somewhere to remind us about this in the future.

Update the comment in go.mod with the new pairing\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"See: https://gitlab.com/cznic/sqlite/-/issues/177\\n\",\n\t\t\tsqliteVersion,\n\t\t\trequiredLibcVersion,\n\t\t\tactualLibcVersion,\n\t\t\trequiredLibcVersion,\n\t\t)\n\t} else {\n\t\tt.Logf(\"\u2713 Version match OK: modernc.org/sqlite@%s requires modernc.org/libc@%s (actual: %s)\",\n\t\t\tsqliteVersion, requiredLibcVersion, actualLibcVersion)\n\t}\n}\n\n// TestGoModCommentUpToDate ensures the comment in go.mod reflects current versions\nfunc TestGoModCommentUpToDate(t *testing.T) {\n\t// Get current sqlite version\n\tcmd := exec.Command(\"go\", \"list\", \"-m\", \"-f\", \"{{.Version}}\", \"modernc.org/sqlite\")\n\toutput, err := cmd.CombinedOutput()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tt.Fatalf(\"Failed to get modernc.org/sqlite version: %v\", err)\n\t}\n\tsqliteVersion := strings.TrimSpace(string(output))\n\n\t// Get current libc version\n\tcmd = exec.Command(\"go\", \"list\", \"-m\", \"-f\", \"{{.Version}}\", \"modernc.org/libc\")\n\toutput, err = cmd.CombinedOutput()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tt.Fatalf(\"Failed to get modernc.org/libc version: %v\", err)\n\t}\n\tlibcVersion := strings.TrimSpace(string(output))\n\n\t// Read go.mod\n\tcmd = exec.Command(\"cat\", \"../../../go.mod\")\n\toutput, err = cmd.CombinedOutput()\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tt.Fatalf(\"Failed to read go.mod: %v\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tgoModContent := string(output)\n\texpectedComment := fmt.Sprintf(\"// Current pairing: sqlite@%s requires libc@%s\", sqliteVersion, libcVersion)\n\n\tif !strings.Contains(goModContent, expectedComment) {\n\t\tt.Errorf(\n\t\t\t\"go.mod comment is out of date!\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Expected to find: %s\\n\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"Please update the comment in go.mod to reflect current versions:\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"  sqlite: %s\\n\"+\n\t\t\t\t\"  libc: %s\\n\",\n\t\t\texpectedComment,\n\t\t\tsqliteVersion,\n\t\t\tlibcVersion,\n\t\t)\n\t}\n}\n"

The user is asking what the second test (TestGoModCommentUpToDate) is doing. Let me explain it clearly.

The second test is checking that the comment in go.mod file is kept up to date with the actual versions of sqlite and libc that are being used.

Specifically, it:

  1. Gets the current version of modernc.org/sqlite
  2. Gets the current version of modernc.org/libc
  3. Reads the go.mod file
  4. Checks if the comment in go.mod contains the expected text like "// Current pairing: sqlite@v1.39.1 requires libc@v1.66.10"

This is to ensure that if someone updates the dependencies, they also update the documentation comment in go.mod to reflect the new pairing. It's a documentation enforcement test.

However, it's currently failing because it's trying to use cat to read the go.mod file, which doesn't work in the test context. I should fix it to use os.ReadFile or similar.

     1‚Üí# Trifle - Browser-based Python3 Playground
     2‚Üí
     3‚ÜíA web application for creating, editing, and running Python3 programs entirely in the browser using Pyodide (WebAssembly Python).
     4‚Üí
     5‚Üí## Project Overview
     6‚Üí
     7‚Üí**Name**: Trifle (individual programs are called "Trifles")
     8‚Üí
     9‚Üí**Core Concept**: Like trinket.io, but:
    10‚Üí- Python3 only (no Python2)
    11‚Üí- Runs entirely in browser via Pyodide
    12‚Üí- Open-source editor (Ace)
    13‚Üí- Restricted to allowlisted users
    14‚Üí- Multiple files per project
    15‚Üí
    16‚Üí## Tech Stack
    17‚Üí
    18‚Üí- **Backend**: Go 1.25+
    19‚Üí- **Frontend**: Vanilla JavaScript (consider htmx if it fits)
    20‚Üí- **Editor**: Ace Editor (from CDN)
    21‚Üí- **Python Runtime**: Pyodide (WebAssembly, from CDN)
    22‚Üí- **Database**: SQLite via `database/sql` + driver (generic SQL, DB-agnostic where possible)
    23‚Üí- **SQL Code Generation**: [sqlc](https://sqlc.dev/) - all SQL in one package, type-safe generated Go code
    24‚Üí- **Database Migrations**: [goose](https://github.com/pressly/goose) - embedded migrations, simple and reliable
    25‚Üí- **Authentication**: Google OAuth 2.0
    26‚Üí- **CSRF Protection**: Go 1.25's built-in CSRF middleware ([reference](https://www.alexedwards.net/blog/preventing-csrf-in-go))
    27‚Üí- **Deployment**: Single Go binary with embedded static files, behind Caddy reverse proxy
    28‚Üí- **Production URL**: https://trifle.greenseptember.com (Caddy terminates TLS)
    29‚Üí
    30‚Üí## Secrets Configuration
    31‚Üí
    32‚ÜíAll secrets stored in 1Password under "Shared/Trifle":
    33‚Üí
    34‚Üí1. **Google OAuth Client Secret**: `op read "op://Shared/Trifle/Google OAuth Client Secret"`
    35‚Üí2. **3DES ID Encryption Key**: `op read "op://Shared/Trifle/3DES ID Key"` (48 hex chars = 24 bytes)
    36‚Üí
    37‚Üí## Google OAuth Configuration
    38‚Üí
    39‚Üí- **Client ID**: `[REDACTED-GOOGLE-CLIENT-ID]`
    40‚Üí- **Development**:
    41‚Üí  - Authorized Origins: `http://localhost:3000`
    42‚Üí  - Redirect URI: `http://localhost:3000/auth/callback`
    43‚Üí- **Production** (will need to add to Google Console):
    44‚Üí  - Authorized Origins: `https://trifle.greenseptember.com`
    45‚Üí  - Redirect URI: `https://trifle.greenseptember.com/auth/callback`
    46‚Üí
    47‚Üí## Data Model
    48‚Üí
    49‚Üí### ID Format Convention
    50‚Üí
    51‚ÜíAll exposed IDs use **Stripe/GitHub-style prefixed random hex strings**:
    52‚Üí
    53‚Üí**Approach**: Generate random hex IDs on creation
    54‚Üí- Generate cryptographically random hex digits
    55‚Üí- Prefix with entity type for type safety and debugging
    56‚Üí- Store full prefixed ID as TEXT PRIMARY KEY in database
    57‚Üí- Retry on collision (extremely rare with sufficient length)
    58‚Üí
    59‚Üí**Format**: `{prefix}_{random_hex}`
    60‚Üí- `trifle_{8_hex}` - Trifle IDs (e.g., `trifle_a3f9c2b8`) - short for nice URLs
    61‚Üí- `account_{12_hex}` - Account IDs (e.g., `account_7b2e8f3a9c1d`)
    62‚Üí- `login_{12_hex}` - Login IDs (e.g., `login_f8a3c2b9e1d4`)
    63‚Üí- `file_{12_hex}` - File IDs (e.g., `file_d4a9b7c3e8f2`)
    64‚Üí
    65‚Üí**Benefits**:
    66‚Üí- Prevents German Tank Problem (random reveals no count info)
    67‚Üí- Type-safe IDs in logs and debugging
    68‚Üí- Flexible lengths per entity type
    69‚Üí- Simple implementation (no crypto needed)
    70‚Üí- Can change approach later if needed
    71‚Üí
    72‚Üí### Tables
    73‚Üí
    74‚Üí#### `logins`
    75‚ÜíRepresents Google OAuth identities
    76‚Üí- `id` - TEXT PRIMARY KEY (e.g., `login_f8a3c2b9e1d4`)
    77‚Üí- `google_id` - TEXT UNIQUE - Google user ID
    78‚Üí- `email` - TEXT - User's email address
    79‚Üí- `name` - TEXT - Display name from Google
    80‚Üí- `created_at` - TIMESTAMP
    81‚Üí
    82‚Üí#### `accounts`
    83‚ÜíRepresents entities that own Trifles (separated from logins for future multi-user support)
    84‚Üí- `id` - TEXT PRIMARY KEY (e.g., `account_7b2e8f3a9c1d`)
    85‚Üí- `display_name` - TEXT UNIQUE - Auto-generated adjective-noun name (e.g., "purple-dinosaur")
    86‚Üí- `created_at` - TIMESTAMP
    87‚Üí- `updated_at` - TIMESTAMP
    88‚Üí
    89‚Üí#### `account_members`
    90‚ÜíLinks logins to accounts (one-to-one in V1, but designed for future multi-user)
    91‚Üí- `id` - TEXT PRIMARY KEY
    92‚Üí- `account_id` - TEXT - Foreign key to accounts
    93‚Üí- `login_id` - TEXT - Foreign key to logins
    94‚Üí- `role` - TEXT - Role string (e.g., "owner", "editor") - just "owner" for V1
    95‚Üí- `created_at` - TIMESTAMP
    96‚Üí- UNIQUE constraint on (account_id, login_id)
    97‚Üí
    98‚Üí#### `trifles`
    99‚ÜíIndividual Python projects/programs
   100‚Üí- `id` - TEXT PRIMARY KEY (e.g., `trifle_a3f9c2b8`)
   101‚Üí- `account_id` - TEXT - Foreign key to accounts
   102‚Üí- `title` - TEXT - User-provided title
   103‚Üí- `description` - TEXT - Optional description (nullable)
   104‚Üí- `parent_id` - TEXT - Foreign key to trifles (for future cloning/remixing, nullable)
   105‚Üí- `created_at` - TIMESTAMP
   106‚Üí- `updated_at` - TIMESTAMP
   107‚Üí
   108‚Üí#### `trifle_files`
   109‚ÜíFiles within a Trifle (supports folders via path)
   110‚Üí- `id` - TEXT PRIMARY KEY (e.g., `file_d4a9b7c3e8f2`)
   111‚Üí- `trifle_id` - TEXT - Foreign key to trifles
   112‚Üí- `path` - TEXT - File path within project (e.g., "main.py", "utils/helper.py")
   113‚Üí- `content` - TEXT - File contents
   114‚Üí- `created_at` - TIMESTAMP
   115‚Üí- `updated_at` - TIMESTAMP
   116‚Üí- UNIQUE constraint on (trifle_id, path)
   117‚Üí
   118‚Üí#### `email_allowlist`
   119‚ÜíControls who can log in
   120‚Üí- `id` - INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT (internal only, never exposed)
   121‚Üí- `pattern` - TEXT - Email or domain pattern (e.g., "[REDACTED-EMAIL]" or "@misstudent.com")
   122‚Üí- `type` - TEXT - "email" or "domain"
   123‚Üí- `created_at` - TIMESTAMP
   124‚Üí- UNIQUE constraint on (pattern, type)
   125‚Üí
   126‚Üí### Initial Allowlist Data
   127‚Üí- Individual email: `[REDACTED-EMAIL]`
   128‚Üí- Domain: `@misstudent.com`
   129‚Üí
   130‚Üí## Architecture
   131‚Üí
   132‚Üí### Backend (Go)
   133‚Üí
   134‚Üí**Pattern**: Single goroutine handles all database access via channels to ensure thread safety.
   135‚Üí
   136‚Üí**Database Access Strategy**:
   137‚Üí- Use [sqlc](https://sqlc.dev/) for type-safe, generated Go code from SQL
   138‚Üí- All SQL queries in one package (`internal/db/queries.sql`)
   139‚Üí- Schema migrations in `internal/db/schema.sql`
   140‚Üí- Generic SQL where possible (avoid SQLite-specific features) for future DB portability
   141‚Üí- Generated code handles parameter binding and row scanning
   142‚Üí
   143‚Üí**Key Components**:
   144‚Üí1. **Database Manager Goroutine**:
   145‚Üí   - Runs in background, receives requests via channel
   146‚Üí   - Executes all SQLite operations using sqlc-generated code
   147‚Üí   - Returns results via response channels
   148‚Üí
   149‚Üí2. **ID Generation**:
   150‚Üí   - Cryptographically random hex strings with type prefixes
   151‚Üí   - Helper functions in `internal/db/ids.go`
   152‚Üí   - Collision retry logic (though extremely rare)
   153‚Üí
   154‚Üí3. **HTTP Server**:
   155‚Üí   - Serves embedded static files
   156‚Üí   - Provides API endpoints
   157‚Üí   - Handles OAuth flow
   158‚Üí   - Uses Go 1.25 CSRF middleware
   159‚Üí
   160‚Üí4. **OAuth Handler**:
   161‚Üí   - Initiates Google OAuth flow
   162‚Üí   - Handles callback
   163‚Üí   - Verifies email against allowlist BEFORE creating session
   164‚Üí   - Creates Login + Account + AccountMember on first login
   165‚Üí   - Generates adjective-noun display name (ensures uniqueness)
   166‚Üí
   167‚Üí5. **Session Management**:
   168‚Üí   - Use secure HTTP-only cookies
   169‚Üí   - Session data in memory (or SQLite if preferred)
   170‚Üí
   171‚Üí### Frontend (Vanilla JS)
   172‚Üí
   173‚Üí**Pages/Views**:
   174‚Üí1. **Login Page**: Google Sign-In button
   175‚Üí2. **Trifle List**: Browse user's Trifles, create new
   176‚Üí3. **Trifle Editor**: Main workspace
   177‚Üí
   178‚Üí**Trifle Editor Layout**:
   179‚Üí```
   180‚Üí+----------------------------------------------------------+
   181‚Üí|  Navbar: [Trifle Logo] [Title]           [User] [Logout]|
   182‚Üí+----------------------------------------------------------+
   183‚Üí| File    |                                                 |
   184‚Üí| Tree    |  Ace Editor                                     |
   185‚Üí|         |  (resizable)                                    |
   186‚Üí|  üìÅ /   |                                                 |
   187‚Üí|  üìÑmain.|                                                 |
   188‚Üí|  üìÑutil.|                                                 |
   189‚Üí|         +--------------------------------------------------+
   190‚Üí|         |  Output Console                                 |
   191‚Üí|         |  (Python stdout/stderr)                         |
   192‚Üí|         |  [Run Button]                                   |
   193‚Üí+---------+--------------------------------------------------+
   194‚Üí```
   195‚Üí
   196‚Üí**Key Frontend Features**:
   197‚Üí- Ace Editor with Python syntax highlighting
   198‚Üí- File tree with add/delete/rename files
   199‚Üí- Resizable editor/console split
   200‚Üí- "Run" button executes main.py via Pyodide
   201‚Üí- Auto-save (debounced, triggers ~1s after typing stops)
   202‚Üí- Load Ace and Pyodide from CDNs
   203‚Üí
   204‚Üí## API Endpoints
   205‚Üí
   206‚Üí### Authentication
   207‚Üí- `GET /auth/login` - Redirect to Google OAuth
   208‚Üí- `GET /auth/callback` - OAuth callback, verify allowlist, create session
   209‚Üí- `POST /auth/logout` - Clear session
   210‚Üí
   211‚Üí### Account Management
   212‚Üí- `POST /api/account/reroll-name` - Generate new display name
   213‚Üí
   214‚Üí### Trifles
   215‚Üí- `GET /api/trifles` - List all user's Trifles
   216‚Üí- `POST /api/trifles` - Create new Trifle (returns ID)
   217‚Üí- `GET /api/trifles/:id` - Get Trifle metadata + all files
   218‚Üí- `PUT /api/trifles/:id` - Update Trifle metadata (title, description)
   219‚Üí- `DELETE /api/trifles/:id` - Delete Trifle
   220‚Üí
   221‚Üí### Trifle Files
   222‚Üí- `GET /api/trifles/:id/files` - List all files in Trifle
   223‚Üí- `PUT /api/trifles/:id/files` - Batch update files (for auto-save)
   224‚Üí- `POST /api/trifles/:id/files` - Create new file
   225‚Üí- `DELETE /api/trifles/:id/files` - Delete file (by path in query param)
   226‚Üí
   227‚Üí## Execution Model
   228‚Üí
   229‚Üí- All Python code runs **client-side** via Pyodide
   230‚Üí- No server-side Python execution
   231‚Üí- Output captured and displayed in console
   232‚Üí- `main.py` is the entry point when "Run" is clicked
   233‚Üí- Future: Support for micropip to install packages
   234‚Üí
   235‚Üí## V1 Scope (MVP)

   349‚Üí## Reference Implementation
   350‚Üí
   351‚ÜíInspiration from: https://github.com/alexprengere/python_playground/blob/main/index.html
   352‚Üí- Single-file example using Ace + Pyodide
   353‚Üí- We'll modernize and split into proper structure
   354‚Üí- Add persistence, auth, multi-file support
   355‚Üí
   356‚Üí## Security Considerations
   357‚Üí
   358‚Üí1. **Allowlist Enforcement**: Check on every login, reject disallowed emails immediately
   359‚Üí2. **Session Security**: HTTP-only, secure cookies (SameSite=Lax or Strict)
   360‚Üí3. **CSRF Protection**: Use Go 1.25's built-in CSRF middleware for all mutating endpoints
   361‚Üí4. **Input Validation**: Validate all API inputs (title lengths, path names, etc.)
   362‚Üí5. **Path Traversal**: Sanitize file paths in Trifles (no `..`, absolute paths, etc.)
   363‚Üí6. **Client-side Execution**: Python runs in browser sandbox (Pyodide), no server-side risk
   364‚Üí7. **Rate Limiting**: Consider adding to prevent abuse
   365‚Üí8. **ID Unpredictability**: Random hex IDs prevent enumeration attacks
   366‚Üí9. **Secrets Management**: All secrets from 1Password, never committed to repo
   367‚Üí
   368‚Üí## Open Questions / Future Considerations
   369‚Üí
   370‚Üí1. Should we add a max Trifle count per account?
   371‚Üí2. Disk space limits per account?
   372‚Üí3. File size limits?
   373‚Üí4. Should adjective-noun list be embedded or configurable?
   374‚Üí5. Session storage: in-memory or SQLite?
   375‚Üí6. How to handle Pyodide version updates?
   376‚Üí7. Admin interface for managing allowlist?
   377‚Üí
   378‚Üí## Notes
   379‚Üí
   380‚Üí- Ace Editor: https://ace.c9.io/ (can load from CDN)
   381‚Üí- Pyodide: https://pyodide.org/ (can load from CDN)
   382‚Üí- Keep UI simple and clean, inspired by trinket.io
   383‚Üí- Auto-save eliminates "run unsaved code" issues
   384‚Üí- Prefixed random hex IDs (Stripe/GitHub style) for type safety and security
   385‚Üí- sqlc generates type-safe Go code from SQL, keeping all SQL in one place
   386‚Üí- Generic SQL approach allows future migration from SQLite if needed

Oh, one question: does Ace include a file browser? Or is it pretty easy to make one?

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:34:38

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 8 in / 8 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

üí≠ Thinking

The user is asking about Ace Editor and whether it includes a file browser. Let me think about what I know about Ace:

Ace Editor is primarily just a code editor component - it's like Monaco Editor or CodeMirror. It handles the text editing, syntax highlighting, themes, etc. But it doesn't include UI chrome like file browsers, toolbars, or project navigation.

For a file browser/tree, we'd need to build that ourselves or use a separate component. There are several options:

  1. Build a simple one with vanilla JS and CSS
  2. Use a library like jstree, fancytree, or similar
  3. Roll our own with just HTML/CSS and some basic JS

Since we're going vanilla JS for this project (as mentioned in the plan), we'd probably want to either build a simple one ourselves or use a lightweight tree component.

Let me check if there's anything specific about Ace and file browsing by searching for it.

Actually, I should just answer based on what I know: Ace is just the editor component, not a full IDE. We'll need to build or integrate a file tree separately.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:34:46

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 8 in / 8 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

Ace Editor is just the code editing component itself - it doesn't include a file browser. It handles syntax highlighting, themes, keybindings, etc., but no UI chrome like file trees or toolbars.

For the file browser, we have a few options:

1. Build it ourselves (vanilla JS + CSS)

  • Pretty straightforward for our use case
  • Just render a <ul> tree from the file list
  • Add click handlers, expand/collapse icons
  • Probably 100-200 lines of JS

2. Use a lightweight tree library

  • jstree - popular, jQuery-based (might want to avoid jQuery)
  • fancytree - similar
  • Various vanilla JS alternatives

3. Simple flat list for MVP

  • Just show all files in a flat list initially
  • Can add folder collapsing later

Given we're going vanilla JS and want to keep it simple, I'd recommend building a basic tree ourselves. It's not complex for our needs:

  • Files come from API as paths like main.py, utils/helper.py
  • Parse paths into tree structure
  • Render with indentation/icons
  • Click to open file in Ace

Want me to add a note about this to CLAUDE.md for future reference?

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:36:40

üí≠ Thinking

Let me check the API endpoints we defined in PLAN.md for file operations...

Looking at the plan:

### Trifle Files
- `GET /api/trifles/:id/files` - List all files in Trifle
- `PUT /api/trifles/:id/files` - Batch update files (for auto-save)
- `POST /api/trifles/:id/files` - Create new file
- `DELETE /api/trifles/:id/files` - Delete file (by path in query param)

So we have:

  • GET /api/trifles/:id/files - Lists all files

But I don't see an endpoint to get a single file by itself. We might want that, or we could just always return all files with their content. Let me also check what we have in the queries.sql:

-- name: GetTrifleFile :one
SELECT * FROM trifle_files
WHERE id = ? LIMIT 1;

-- name: GetTrifleFileByPath :one
SELECT * FROM trifle_files
WHERE trifle_id = ? AND path = ?
LIMIT 1;

-- name: ListTrifleFilesByTrifleID :many
SELECT * FROM trifle_files
WHERE trifle_id = ?
ORDER BY path;

So we have database queries for:

  1. List all files in a trifle (with full content) - ListTrifleFilesByTrifleID
  2. Get a single file by path - GetTrifleFileByPath
  3. Get a single file by ID - GetTrifleFile

But in the API endpoints, we only have the list endpoint. The user is asking if we can get individual files.

Options:

  1. Always return all files with content when listing (might be fine for V1 if projects are small)
  2. Add an endpoint to get a single file: GET /api/trifles/:id/files/:path or GET /api/trifles/:id/files?path=xxx

For student-focused projects with compact codebases, bulk file retrieval seems pragmatic. The simplicity of returning all files at once could outweigh the need for granular file fetching. Performance won't be a significant concern with smaller project sizes, making this approach both efficient and straightforward.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:36:43

Model: claude-sonnet-4-5-20250929 Tokens: 8 in / 892 out Working Dir: /Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit

Looking at the API endpoints in PLAN.md:

### Trifle Files
- `GET /api/trifles/:id/files` - List all files in Trifle
- `PUT /api/trifles/:id/files` - Batch update files (for auto-save)
- `POST /api/trifles/:id/files` - Create new file
- `DELETE /api/trifles/:id/files` - Delete file (by path in query param)

We have GET /api/trifles/:id/files for listing, but the description doesn't specify if it includes file content or just the file list.

In the database queries (queries.sql), we have:

  • ListTrifleFilesByTrifleID - returns all files including content
  • GetTrifleFileByPath - returns a single file by path

Two options:

  1. Simple (good for V1): GET /api/trifles/:id/files returns all files WITH content. Small student projects won't have performance issues.

  2. Optimized:

    • GET /api/trifles/:id/files returns just metadata (paths, ids)
    • Add GET /api/trifles/:id/files/:path to fetch individual file content

For V1 with small projects, I'd recommend option 1 - simpler, fewer round trips, and performance should be fine. We can optimize later if needed.

Should I update PLAN.md to clarify this?

    46‚Üí
    47‚Üí	log.Println("Database initialized successfully")
    48‚Üí
    49‚Üí	// Initialize session manager
    50‚Üí	sessionMgr := auth.NewSessionManager(isProduction)
    51‚Üí
    52‚Üí	// Get OAuth credentials
    53‚Üí	clientID, clientSecret, err := auth.GetOAuthCredentials()
    54‚Üí	if err != nil {
    55‚Üí		log.Fatalf("Failed to get OAuth credentials: %v", err)
    56‚Üí	}
    57‚Üí
    58‚Üí	// Determine redirect URL based on environment
    59‚Üí	redirectURL := fmt.Sprintf("http://localhost:%s/auth/callback", port)
    60‚Üí	if isProduction {
    61‚Üí		redirectURL = "https://trifle.greenseptember.com/auth/callback"
    62‚Üí	}
    63‚Üí
    64‚Üí	// Initialize OAuth config
    65‚Üí	oauthConfig := auth.NewOAuthConfig(clientID, clientSecret, redirectURL, dbManager, sessionMgr)
    66‚Üí
    67‚Üí	// Set up HTTP router
    68‚Üí	mux := http.NewServeMux()
    69‚Üí
    70‚Üí	// Auth routes
    71‚Üí	mux.HandleFunc("/auth/login", oauthConfig.HandleLogin)
    72‚Üí	mux.HandleFunc("/auth/callback", oauthConfig.HandleCallback)
    73‚Üí	mux.HandleFunc("/auth/logout", oauthConfig.HandleLogout)
    74‚Üí
    75‚Üí	// Serve static files from embedded web directory
    76‚Üí	webContent, err := fs.Sub(webFS, "web")
    77‚Üí	if err != nil {
    78‚Üí		log.Fatalf("Failed to get web subdirectory: %v", err)
    79‚Üí	}
    80‚Üí	fileServer := http.FileServer(http.FS(webContent))
    81‚Üí	mux.Handle("/", fileServer)
    82‚Üí
    83‚Üí	// Create HTTP server
    84‚Üí	server := &http.Server{
    85‚Üí		Addr:         fmt.Sprintf(":%s", port),
    86‚Üí		Handler:      mux,
    87‚Üí		ReadTimeout:  15 * time.Second,
    88‚Üí		WriteTimeout: 15 * time.Second,
    89‚Üí		IdleTimeout:  60 * time.Second,
    90‚Üí	}
    91‚Üí
    92‚Üí	// Start server in goroutine
    93‚Üí	go func() {
    94‚Üí		log.Printf("Trifle server starting on http://localhost:%s", port)
    95‚Üí		if err := server.ListenAndServe(); err != nil && err != http.ErrServerClosed {
    96‚Üí			log.Fatalf("Server failed: %v", err)
    97‚Üí		}
    98‚Üí	}()
    99‚Üí
   100‚Üí	// Wait for interrupt signal
   101‚Üí	sigCh := make(chan os.Signal, 1)
   102‚Üí	signal.Notify(sigCh, syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM)
   103‚Üí	<-sigCh
   104‚Üí
   105‚Üí	log.Println("Shutting down server...")
   106‚Üí
   107‚Üí	// Graceful shutdown
   108‚Üí	ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 15*time.Second)
   109‚Üí	defer cancel()
   110‚Üí
   111‚Üí	if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {
   112‚Üí		log.Printf("Server shutdown error: %v", err)
   113‚Üí	}
   114‚Üí
   115‚Üí	log.Println("Server stopped")
   116‚Üí}

  1. The OAuth error "invalid_grant" might be because the redirect URI doesn't match or there's a timing issue
  2. The panic is because GetLoginByGoogleID is returning db.Login (value) instead of *db.Login (pointer)

Let me fix the panic first - it's in manager.go:120. Looking at the code:

func (m *Manager) GetLoginByGoogleID(ctx context.Context, googleID string) (*Login, error) {
	result, err := m.execute(func(db *sql.DB, q *Queries) (interface{}, error) {
		return q.GetLoginByGoogleID(ctx, googleID)
	})
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}
	return result.(*Login), nil
}

The issue is that q.GetLoginByGoogleID likely returns a Login value, not a pointer. Let me check what sqlc generates...

Actually, I need to look at what sqlc generated. The query was:

-- name: GetLoginByGoogleID :one
SELECT * FROM logins
WHERE google_id = ? LIMIT 1;

With :one, sqlc typically returns a struct value, not a pointer. So we need to handle it differently. We could either:

  1. Return the value and then take its address
  2. Change the sqlc comment to return a pointer (if that's an option)

Let me fix this by properly handling the return type.

ü§ñ ASSISTANT ‚Äî 2025-10-19 02:57:57

üí≠ Thinking

The user is saying that when they click the login button, it briefly goes to accounts.google.com and then comes back to the same screen with the login button again. This suggests:

  1. The OAuth redirect is happening
  2. Google is redirecting back
  3. But something in the callback handler is failing and redirecting back to the landing page

Looking at the callback handler in oauth.go, there are several places where we redirect back to "/" on error:

  • Invalid session
  • Invalid state
  • Missing code
  • Failed token exchange
  • Unverified email
  • Email not on allowlist
  • Various other failures

But we're not logging or showing any error messages to the user. The callback handler just does http.Error() which shows an error page, or redirects to "/" on success.

Wait, I see the issue. After a successful login, we redirect to "/" which is the landing page! We need to:

  1. Check if the user is already authenticated on the landing page
  2. If so, redirect them to a logged-in view (like /trifles or /dashboard)
  3. OR make the landing page show different content when logged in

Let me check what's happening - we should add some logging to see which error path is being hit.

It sounds like the OAuth flow is starting but then immediately redirecting back to the landing page. This usually means an error in the callback handler is silently failing. The issue is we're using http.Error() which might not be visible, and on success we redirect to "/" which is still the landing page!

Let me add logging and fix the redirect:

    97‚Üí	}
    98‚Üí
    99‚Üí	// Verify state token (CSRF protection)
   100‚Üí	state := r.URL.Query().Get("state")
   101‚Üí	if state == "" || state != session.OAuthState {
   102‚Üí		log.Printf("State mismatch: got %q, expected %q", state, session.OAuthState)
   103‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Invalid state parameter - please try logging in again", http.StatusBadRequest)
   104‚Üí		return
   105‚Üí	}
   106‚Üí
   107‚Üí	// Exchange code for token
   108‚Üí	code := r.URL.Query().Get("code")
   109‚Üí	if code == "" {
   110‚Üí		log.Printf("No code in callback")
   111‚Üí		http.Error(w, "No authorization code received", http.StatusBadRequest)
   112‚Üí		return
   113‚Üí	}
   114‚Üí
   115‚Üí	token, err := oc.Config.Exchange(ctx, code)
   116‚Üí	if err != nil {
   117‚Üí		log.Printf("Failed to exchange token: %v", err)
   118‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to exchange token: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   119‚Üí		return
   120‚Üí	}
   121‚Üí
   122‚Üí	// Get user info from Google
   123‚Üí	userInfo, err := oc.getUserInfo(ctx, token)
   124‚Üí	if err != nil {
   125‚Üí		log.Printf("Failed to get user info: %v", err)
   126‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to get user info: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   127‚Üí		return
   128‚Üí	}
   129‚Üí
   130‚Üí	log.Printf("User attempting to log in: %s (%s)", userInfo.Email, userInfo.Name)
   131‚Üí
   132‚Üí	// Check if email is verified
   133‚Üí	if !userInfo.VerifiedEmail {
   134‚Üí		log.Printf("Email not verified: %s", userInfo.Email)
   135‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Email not verified with Google", http.StatusForbidden)
   136‚Üí		return
   137‚Üí	}
   138‚Üí
   139‚Üí	// Check allowlist
   140‚Üí	allowed, err := oc.DBManager.CheckEmailAllowlist(ctx, userInfo.Email)
   141‚Üí	if err != nil {
   142‚Üí		log.Printf("Failed to check allowlist: %v", err)
   143‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to check allowlist", http.StatusInternalServerError)
   144‚Üí		return
   145‚Üí	}
   146‚Üí	if !allowed {
   147‚Üí		log.Printf("Email not on allowlist: %s", userInfo.Email)
   148‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Access denied: email not on allowlist", http.StatusForbidden)
   149‚Üí		return
   150‚Üí	}
   151‚Üí
   152‚Üí	// Get or create login
   153‚Üí	login, err := oc.getOrCreateLogin(ctx, userInfo)
   154‚Üí	if err != nil {
   155‚Üí		log.Printf("Failed to process login: %v", err)
   156‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to process login: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   157‚Üí		return
   158‚Üí	}
   159‚Üí
   160‚Üí	// Get the user's account
   161‚Üí	account, err := oc.getAccountForLogin(ctx, login.ID)
   162‚Üí	if err != nil {
   163‚Üí		log.Printf("Failed to get account: %v", err)
   164‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to get account: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   165‚Üí		return
   166‚Üí	}
   167‚Üí
   168‚Üí	log.Printf("Login successful: %s (account: %s - %s)", userInfo.Email, account.ID, account.DisplayName)
   169‚Üí
   170‚Üí	// Update session with login info
   171‚Üí	session.LoginID = login.ID
   172‚Üí	session.AccountID = account.ID
   173‚Üí	session.Email = login.Email
   174‚Üí	session.Authenticated = true
   175‚Üí	session.OAuthState = "" // Clear the state token
   176‚Üí
   177‚Üí	if err := oc.SessionMgr.Save(w, session); err != nil {
   178‚Üí		log.Printf("Failed to save session: %v", err)
   179‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to save session", http.StatusInternalServerError)
   180‚Üí		return
   181‚Üí	}
   182‚Üí
   183‚Üí	// Redirect to logged-in home page
   184‚Üí	// TODO: For now redirect to /, but we'll make the landing page show different content when logged in
   185‚Üí	http.Redirect(w, r, "/", http.StatusSeeOther)
   186‚Üí}

    81‚Üí// HandleCallback processes the OAuth callback from Google
    82‚Üífunc (oc *OAuthConfig) HandleCallback(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
    83‚Üí	ctx := r.Context()
    84‚Üí
    85‚Üí	// Check for error from Google
    86‚Üí	if errMsg := r.URL.Query().Get("error"); errMsg != "" {
    87‚Üí		slog.Error("OAuth error from Google", "error", errMsg)
    88‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("OAuth error: %s", errMsg), http.StatusBadRequest)
    89‚Üí		return
    90‚Üí	}
    91‚Üí
    92‚Üí	// Get the session to verify state
    93‚Üí	session, err := oc.SessionMgr.GetSession(r)
    94‚Üí	if err != nil || session == nil {
    95‚Üí		slog.Warn("Invalid session in callback", "error", err)
    96‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Invalid session - please try logging in again", http.StatusBadRequest)
    97‚Üí		return
    98‚Üí	}
    99‚Üí
   100‚Üí	// Verify state token (CSRF protection)
   101‚Üí	state := r.URL.Query().Get("state")
   102‚Üí	if state == "" || state != session.OAuthState {
   103‚Üí		slog.Warn("State mismatch", "got", state, "expected", session.OAuthState)
   104‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Invalid state parameter - please try logging in again", http.StatusBadRequest)
   105‚Üí		return
   106‚Üí	}
   107‚Üí
   108‚Üí	// Exchange code for token
   109‚Üí	code := r.URL.Query().Get("code")
   110‚Üí	if code == "" {
   111‚Üí		slog.Warn("No code in callback")
   112‚Üí		http.Error(w, "No authorization code received", http.StatusBadRequest)
   113‚Üí		return
   114‚Üí	}
   115‚Üí
   116‚Üí	token, err := oc.Config.Exchange(ctx, code)
   117‚Üí	if err != nil {
   118‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to exchange token", "error", err)
   119‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to exchange token: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   120‚Üí		return
   121‚Üí	}
   122‚Üí
   123‚Üí	// Get user info from Google
   124‚Üí	userInfo, err := oc.getUserInfo(ctx, token)
   125‚Üí	if err != nil {
   126‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to get user info", "error", err)
   127‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to get user info: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   128‚Üí		return
   129‚Üí	}
   130‚Üí
   131‚Üí	slog.Info("User attempting to log in", "email", userInfo.Email, "name", userInfo.Name)
   132‚Üí
   133‚Üí	// Check if email is verified
   134‚Üí	if !userInfo.VerifiedEmail {
   135‚Üí		slog.Warn("Email not verified", "email", userInfo.Email)
   136‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Email not verified with Google", http.StatusForbidden)
   137‚Üí		return
   138‚Üí	}
   139‚Üí
   140‚Üí	// Check allowlist
   141‚Üí	allowed, err := oc.DBManager.CheckEmailAllowlist(ctx, userInfo.Email)
   142‚Üí	if err != nil {
   143‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to check allowlist", "error", err)
   144‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to check allowlist", http.StatusInternalServerError)
   145‚Üí		return
   146‚Üí	}
   147‚Üí	if !allowed {
   148‚Üí		slog.Warn("Email not on allowlist", "email", userInfo.Email)
   149‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Access denied: email not on allowlist", http.StatusForbidden)
   150‚Üí		return
   151‚Üí	}

   157‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to process login: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   158‚Üí		return
   159‚Üí	}
   160‚Üí

   164‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to get account", "error", err)

{
  "file_path": "/Users/zellyn/gh/trunkit/internal/api/middleware.go",
  "content": "package api\n\nimport (\n\t\"log/slog\"\n\t\"net/http\"\n\t\"time\"\n)\n\n// responseWriter wraps http.ResponseWriter to capture the status code\ntype responseWriter struct {\n\thttp.ResponseWriter\n\tstatusCode int\n\twritten    int\n}\n\nfunc (rw *responseWriter) WriteHeader(code int) {\n\trw.statusCode = code\n\trw.ResponseWriter.WriteHeader(code)\n}\n\nfunc (rw *responseWriter) Write(b []byte) (int, error) {\n\tn, err := rw.ResponseWriter.Write(b)\n\trw.written += n\n\treturn n, err\n}\n\n// LoggingMiddleware logs HTTP requests in a standard format\nfunc LoggingMiddleware(next http.Handler) http.Handler {\n\treturn http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n\t\tstart := time.Now()\n\n\t\t// Wrap the response writer to capture status code\n\t\twrapped := &responseWriter{\n\t\t\tResponseWriter: w,\n\t\t\tstatusCode:     200, // default status code\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Call the next handler\n\t\tnext.ServeHTTP(wrapped, r)\n\n\t\t// Log the request\n\t\tduration := time.Since(start)\n\t\tslog.Info(\"HTTP request\",\n\t\t\t\"method\", r.Method,\n\t\t\t\"path\", r.URL.Path,\n\t\t\t\"status\", wrapped.statusCode,\n\t\t\t\"duration_ms\", duration.Milliseconds(),\n\t\t\t\"bytes\", wrapped.written,\n\t\t\t\"remote_addr\", r.RemoteAddr,\n\t\t)\n\t})\n}\n"
}

    54‚Üí
    55‚Üí// HandleLogin redirects the user to Google's OAuth consent page
    56‚Üífunc (oc *OAuthConfig) HandleLogin(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
    57‚Üí	// Generate a random state token for CSRF protection
    58‚Üí	state, err := generateRandomString(32)
    59‚Üí	if err != nil {
    60‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to generate state token", http.StatusInternalServerError)
    61‚Üí		return
    62‚Üí	}
    63‚Üí
    64‚Üí	// Store state in session (we'll verify it in the callback)
    65‚Üí	session, err := oc.SessionMgr.GetOrCreateSession(r, w)
    66‚Üí	if err != nil {
    67‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to create session", http.StatusInternalServerError)
    68‚Üí		return
    69‚Üí	}
    70‚Üí	session.OAuthState = state
    71‚Üí	if err := oc.SessionMgr.Save(w, session); err != nil {
    72‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to save session", http.StatusInternalServerError)
    73‚Üí		return
    74‚Üí	}
    75‚Üí
    76‚Üí	// Redirect to Google's consent page
    77‚Üí	url := oc.Config.AuthCodeURL(state, oauth2.AccessTypeOffline)
    78‚Üí	http.Redirect(w, r, url, http.StatusTemporaryRedirect)
    79‚Üí}
    80‚Üí
    81‚Üí// HandleCallback processes the OAuth callback from Google
    82‚Üífunc (oc *OAuthConfig) HandleCallback(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
    83‚Üí	ctx := r.Context()
    84‚Üí
    85‚Üí	// Check for error from Google
    86‚Üí	if errMsg := r.URL.Query().Get("error"); errMsg != "" {
    87‚Üí		slog.Error("OAuth error from Google", "error", errMsg)
    88‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("OAuth error: %s", errMsg), http.StatusBadRequest)
    89‚Üí		return
    90‚Üí	}
    91‚Üí
    92‚Üí	// Get the session to verify state
    93‚Üí	session, err := oc.SessionMgr.GetSession(r)
    94‚Üí	if err != nil || session == nil {
    95‚Üí		slog.Warn("Invalid session in callback", "error", err)
    96‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Invalid session - please try logging in again", http.StatusBadRequest)
    97‚Üí		return
    98‚Üí	}
    99‚Üí
   100‚Üí	// Verify state token (CSRF protection)
   101‚Üí	state := r.URL.Query().Get("state")
   102‚Üí	if state == "" || state != session.OAuthState {
   103‚Üí		slog.Warn("State mismatch", "got", state, "expected", session.OAuthState)
   104‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Invalid state parameter - please try logging in again", http.StatusBadRequest)
   105‚Üí		return
   106‚Üí	}
   107‚Üí
   108‚Üí	// Exchange code for token
   109‚Üí	code := r.URL.Query().Get("code")
   110‚Üí	if code == "" {
   111‚Üí		slog.Warn("No code in callback")
   112‚Üí		http.Error(w, "No authorization code received", http.StatusBadRequest)
   113‚Üí		return
   114‚Üí	}
   115‚Üí
   116‚Üí	token, err := oc.Config.Exchange(ctx, code)
   117‚Üí	if err != nil {
   118‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to exchange token", "error", err)
   119‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to exchange token: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   120‚Üí		return
   121‚Üí	}
   122‚Üí
   123‚Üí	// Get user info from Google
   124‚Üí	userInfo, err := oc.getUserInfo(ctx, token)
   125‚Üí	if err != nil {
   126‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to get user info", "error", err)
   127‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to get user info: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   128‚Üí		return
   129‚Üí	}
   130‚Üí
   131‚Üí	slog.Info("User attempting to log in", "email", userInfo.Email, "name", userInfo.Name)
   132‚Üí
   133‚Üí	// Check if email is verified
   134‚Üí	if !userInfo.VerifiedEmail {
   135‚Üí		slog.Warn("Email not verified", "email", userInfo.Email)
   136‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Email not verified with Google", http.StatusForbidden)
   137‚Üí		return
   138‚Üí	}
   139‚Üí
   140‚Üí	// Check allowlist
   141‚Üí	allowed, err := oc.DBManager.CheckEmailAllowlist(ctx, userInfo.Email)
   142‚Üí	if err != nil {
   143‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to check allowlist", "error", err)
   144‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to check allowlist", http.StatusInternalServerError)
   145‚Üí		return
   146‚Üí	}
   147‚Üí	if !allowed {
   148‚Üí		slog.Warn("Email not on allowlist", "email", userInfo.Email)
   149‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Access denied: email not on allowlist", http.StatusForbidden)
   150‚Üí		return
   151‚Üí	}
   152‚Üí
   153‚Üí	// Get or create login
   154‚Üí	login, err := oc.getOrCreateLogin(ctx, userInfo)
   155‚Üí	if err != nil {
   156‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to process login", "error", err)
   157‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to process login: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   158‚Üí		return
   159‚Üí	}
   160‚Üí
   161‚Üí	// Get the user's account
   162‚Üí	account, err := oc.getAccountForLogin(ctx, login.ID)
   163‚Üí	if err != nil {
   164‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to get account", "error", err)
   165‚Üí		http.Error(w, fmt.Sprintf("Failed to get account: %v", err), http.StatusInternalServerError)
   166‚Üí		return
   167‚Üí	}
   168‚Üí
   169‚Üí	slog.Info("Login successful", "email", userInfo.Email, "account_id", account.ID, "display_name", account.DisplayName)
   170‚Üí
   171‚Üí	// Update session with login info
   172‚Üí	session.LoginID = login.ID
   173‚Üí	session.AccountID = account.ID
   174‚Üí	session.Email = login.Email
   175‚Üí	session.Authenticated = true
   176‚Üí	session.OAuthState = "" // Clear the state token
   177‚Üí
   178‚Üí	if err := oc.SessionMgr.Save(w, session); err != nil {
   179‚Üí		slog.Error("Failed to save session", "error", err)
   180‚Üí		http.Error(w, "Failed to save session", http.StatusInternalServerError)
   181‚Üí		return
   182‚Üí	}
   183‚Üí
   184‚Üí	// Redirect to logged-in home page
   185‚Üí	// TODO: For now redirect to /, but we'll make the landing page show different content when logged in
   186‚Üí	http.Redirect(w, r, "/", http.StatusSeeOther)
   187‚Üí}

   189‚Üí// getUserInfo fetches user information from Google

   211‚Üí// getOrCreateLogin retrieves an existing login or creates a new one
   212‚Üífunc (oc *OAuthConfig) getOrCreateLogin(ctx context.Context, userInfo *GoogleUser) (*db.Login, error) {
   213‚Üí	// Try to get existing login by Google ID
   214‚Üí	login, err := oc.DBManager.GetLoginByGoogleID(ctx, userInfo.ID)
   215‚Üí	if err == nil {
   216‚Üí		// Login exists, update email/name in case they changed
   217‚Üí		// (Note: We don't expose UpdateLogin via Manager yet, skipping for now)
   218‚Üí		return login, nil
   219‚Üí	}
   220‚Üí
   221‚Üí	if err != sql.ErrNoRows {
   222‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to query login: %w", err)
   223‚Üí	}
   224‚Üí
   225‚Üí	// Login doesn't exist, create new login + account + account_member in a transaction
   226‚Üí	loginID, err := db.NewLoginID()
   227‚Üí	if err != nil {
   228‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to generate login ID: %w", err)
   229‚Üí	}
   230‚Üí
   231‚Üí	accountID, err := db.NewAccountID()
   232‚Üí	if err != nil {
   233‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to generate account ID: %w", err)
   234‚Üí	}
   235‚Üí
   236‚Üí	accountMemberID, err := db.NewAccountID() // Reuse same ID generator
   237‚Üí	if err != nil {
   238‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to generate account member ID: %w", err)
   239‚Üí	}
   240‚Üí
   241‚Üí	// Generate unique display name
   242‚Üí	displayName, err := oc.generateUniqueDisplayName(ctx)
   243‚Üí	if err != nil {
   244‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to generate display name: %w", err)
   245‚Üí	}
   246‚Üí
   247‚Üí	// Create login, account, and account_member in a transaction
   248‚Üí	err = oc.DBManager.Transaction(ctx, func(tx *sql.Tx, q *db.Queries) error {
   249‚Üí		// Create login
   250‚Üí		if err := q.CreateLogin(ctx, db.CreateLoginParams{
   251‚Üí			ID:       loginID,
   252‚Üí			GoogleID: userInfo.ID,
   253‚Üí			Email:    userInfo.Email,
   254‚Üí			Name:     userInfo.Name,
   255‚Üí		}); err != nil {
   256‚Üí			return fmt.Errorf("failed to create login: %w", err)
   257‚Üí		}
   258‚Üí
   259‚Üí		// Create account
   260‚Üí		if err := q.CreateAccount(ctx, db.CreateAccountParams{
   261‚Üí			ID:          accountID,
   262‚Üí			DisplayName: displayName,
   263‚Üí		}); err != nil {
   264‚Üí			return fmt.Errorf("failed to create account: %w", err)
   265‚Üí		}
   266‚Üí
   267‚Üí		// Create account member
   268‚Üí		if err := q.CreateAccountMember(ctx, db.CreateAccountMemberParams{
   269‚Üí			ID:        accountMemberID,
   270‚Üí			AccountID: accountID,
   271‚Üí			LoginID:   loginID,
   272‚Üí			Role:      "owner",
   273‚Üí		}); err != nil {
   274‚Üí			return fmt.Errorf("failed to create account member: %w", err)
   275‚Üí		}
   276‚Üí
   277‚Üí		return nil
   278‚Üí	})
   279‚Üí
   280‚Üí	if err != nil {
   281‚Üí		return nil, err
   282‚Üí	}
   283‚Üí
   284‚Üí	// Fetch and return the newly created login
   285‚Üí	return oc.DBManager.GetLoginByGoogleID(ctx, userInfo.ID)
   286‚Üí}
   287‚Üí
   288‚Üí// generateUniqueDisplayName generates a unique display name, retrying if there's a collision
   289‚Üífunc (oc *OAuthConfig) generateUniqueDisplayName(ctx context.Context) (string, error) {
   290‚Üí	const maxRetries = 10
   291‚Üí
   292‚Üí	for i := 0; i < maxRetries; i++ {
   293‚Üí		name, err := namegen.Generate()
   294‚Üí		if err != nil {
   295‚Üí			return "", err
   296‚Üí		}
   297‚Üí
   298‚Üí		// Check if name is already taken
   299‚Üí		_, err = oc.DBManager.GetAccountByDisplayName(ctx, name)
   300‚Üí		if err == sql.ErrNoRows {
   301‚Üí			// Name is available!
   302‚Üí			return name, nil
   303‚Üí		}
   304‚Üí		if err != nil {
   305‚Üí			return "", fmt.Errorf("failed to check display name: %w", err)
   306‚Üí		}
   307‚Üí
   308‚Üí		// Name is taken, try again
   309‚Üí	}
   310‚Üí
   311‚Üí	return "", fmt.Errorf("failed to generate unique display name after %d attempts", maxRetries)
   312‚Üí}
   313‚Üí
   314‚Üí// getAccountForLogin retrieves the account associated with a login
   315‚Üífunc (oc *OAuthConfig) getAccountForLogin(ctx context.Context, loginID string) (*db.Account, error) {
   316‚Üí	// Get account members for this login
   317‚Üí	members, err := oc.DBManager.GetAccountMembersByLoginID(ctx, loginID)

   319‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("failed to get account members: %w", err)
   320‚Üí	}

   323‚Üí		return nil, fmt.Errorf("no account found for login")
   324‚Üí	}

   327‚Üí	return oc.DBManager.GetAccount(ctx, members[0].AccountID)
   328‚Üí}
